The information contained in this directory was compiled by the Personnel OfficeandtheStudent Government of the University of Notre Dame. Student ad­dresses are those that were turned in at registration or corrected at the Student GovernmentOfficebeforeOctober2, 1965. Personswishing to make corrections shouldsendtheirname, address andthe correction to either the Student Govern­ment Office or Personnel Office, c/o Student-Staff-Faculty Directory. If suf­ficientcorrectionsarereceived, a supplement to this Directory willbe published later this year.

Operating Instructions for Centrex 
Operating 


ON CAMPUS -Dialthedesiredfour-digitnum­ber as indicated in this directory. 
FROM OFF CAMPUS -Dial 284 plus the de­sired extension as listed in this directory. 
LOCAL -Dial ”9" for outside line, then dial numberaslisted in the SouthBend-Mishawaka directory. 
LONGDISTANCE -Onall long-distance calls, whenthe operator asks for your number, give her 284 and the number assigned to you. Do not give 284-6011. 
Station-to-Station -Dial "9" for outside line, thendial”1" for direct distance dialing equip­mentthen dial the area code and identification number of the distant party. 
Person-to-person -Dial ”9" for outside line, then dial ”0" for Indiana Bell operator, give her the area code, telephone number and the person you wish to contact. 
INFORMATION -For University numbers not listed in your Notre Dame directory dial "0" for your information operator. For numbers notlistedinthe SouthBend directory, dial "9" then "113" for an Indiana Bell operator. 
REPAIRSERVICE -Ifyourphone'is not work­ing properly, go to another nearby telephone, dial"0" for your Notre Dame switchboard op­erator and report it to her. 
CONFERENCE CALLS can be placedfrom anystation on campus by dialing "5" for the con­ference operator. Itispossible to have 5 con­ferees on one conference call. 
TRANSFERRING INCOMING calls to another station on the campus can be accomplished bydepressingtheplungercompletely down. Hold in this position for about 2 seconds -release and you will receive a ring. Wait for the op­erator to answer andgive herthe stationnum­ber or party where tfie call should be trans­ferred. The aboveprocedure mustbe done on the line that the incoming call originates. Do not go to another line and dial "0" for the op­erator. Transfer and incoming calls are an­sweredinthe sequence that they are received. Do nothang upif the operator does not answer immediately. 
DIRECTORY CHANGES should be reported as they occur to the Personnel Department. Changes include additions, deletions, number changes, etc. 
TO REPORT AN EMERGENCY -Dial "0" op­erator and give location of accident, name of injuredperson, if known,and extension of cal­ling party. Calling party should stay on the lineuntilthe operator has made arrangements for the ambulance. 
Individuals in need of ambulance service for reason of illness should contact a private am­bulance. Suggested ambulances are: 
Hickey 234-4155 Walsh-Bilancio 232-5853 
TO CALL YOU -Those off campus will need theentire seven-figure number ofyour phone. Please send it to them. Cards are provided withoutcharge. If you need more, they can be obtained from the Personnel Office. 
TOSPEEDYOURCALLS-Long-distancecalls will go through twice as fast if you give the Indiana Bell operatorthe area code for the city and the number of the phone you are calling. Personal long-distance calls are to be made from campusphones onlyin an emergency and suchcalls mustbe charged to your home tele­phone.

Recognition of Responsibility 
The Honor Code adopted by the University of Notre Dame sets high standards of conduct for the members of the student body. It is a formal recognition of the ability of students to take responsibility and as such is based on two simple principles: 1) That as a member of the academic community, a student will be responsible for his own work, and 2) He will expect the same academic honesty of his fellow students. A further purpose is to create a greater awareness in each student of this responsibility both to himself and to his fellow students. The fact that a young man is a student at the Uni­versity of Notre Dame is enough to expect that he is honest and will abide by the Honor Code and no written pledge as such is de­manded at any time. 
Execution of Responsibility 
The student body, with the approval of the Academic Council of the University, has accepted this responsibility of maintaining in­tegrity in the classroom. As an official recognition of this acceptance, the Student Honor Council of twenty-five members selected by the student representatives has been formed to maintain the provisions of the Honor Code. The Council handles all reported violations of the Honor Code and conducts trials whenever necessary. It is also their responsibility to investigate and propose to the Student Senate any changes to be made in the provisions of the Honor Code and to coordinate and consult with the faculty and administration concern­ing its operation. 
Academic 

The Honor Code has been written to cover all academic work submitted by students for credit. Distinct moral standards are often difficult to determine especially among a large group of young men with varied interests. Standards of conduct in the classroom, on the other hand, are universally accepted; one either does his own work or he does not. This fact is basic. Each student is attending the Uni­versity to learn and to meet the requirements for a degree. If a stu­dent is not honest in his classwork, which undeniably determines a great deal of his future, it makes little difference that he should be honest elsewhere. The spirit of integrity should not be limited only to the classroom, however, but should pervade all that a student does both during and after his days at Notre Dame. 
Faculty 

All important to the success of the Honor Code is the cooperation between faculty and students. As a guiding member of the academic community, each instructor plays a major role by placing his trust in his students andby encouraging similar trust among the students themselves. Such a mutual trust leads to closer understanding be­tween instructor and student and creates a classroom atmosphere more conducive to fellowship and learning. An atmosphere pervaded by such trust cannot help but contribute to the greatness of Notre Dame as an academic institution. 
Christian Spirit 
The Honor Code is not proposed as a cure-all for every academic problem. Nor is it simply the replacing of one “proctor” system with another. It is not a spy system where students are encouraged to tell on one another. Rather, the Honor Code depends on the good will and Christian spirit of each student to care enough for a friend or a fellow student, even though a stranger, to warn him to quit cheating for his own sake and that of the community. By encourag­ing good will and pride among the Student Body, the Honor Code reflects the responsibility to be assumed by each student, a responsi­bility which is vital to its success. 
Characteristic of Notre Dame 
The Honor Code draws special strength from the fact that Notre 
Dame is unique as a university. Every year students from all parts 
of the country who share in approximately the same social, if not 
religious, backgrounds come to Notre Dame. These are the young 
men who determine the characteristics of the Honor Code which are 
the same as those of the University itself; the spirit of fellowship, 
fierce personal pride, and the general Christian atmosphere. These 
characteristics in turn reflect the high standards in every University 
activity. 
Challenge 

To maintain honesty of the highest standards under the pressures 
of modern society is admittedly difficult but as long as those students 
who participate in the Code are prepared to face the difficulties and 
commit themselves to the idea of honesty, complete success of the 
Honor Code is assured. 
Article I PLEDGE: 

The undergraduate student body of the University of Notre Dame, united in a spirit of mutual trust and fellowship, mindful of the values of a true education and the challenge posed by the mod­ern world to the integrity of Christian gentlemen, do hereby pledge ourselves to accept the responsibilities for honorable conduct in all academic activities, to assist one another in maintaining and promot­ing personal integrity, and to abide by the principles and proce­dures set forth in this Honor Code. 
Article II PRINCIPLES: 
A. All work submitted for credit in any form shall be the result 01 
the student’s own thought and honest effort according to proce­dures established in the couise. 
B. Each student shall be responsible not only for maintaining his own honor, but also for demanding honor among his fellow stu­dents. He shall consider himself a part of the community of honor, and, if that honor is violated, it is his responsibility to restore that community through the means of the Honor Code. 
C. In the spirit of mutual cooperation, understanding, and respect among students, faculty, and administration, students shall have authority to govern themselves under this Honor Code. 
Article HI JURISDICTION: 
The pledge shall pertain to activities directly related to the pursuit of formal studies, both inside and outside the classroom. Specifically this shall include: 
1. 
Exams of all types 

2. 
Class work 

3. 
Papers and reports 


Article IV IMPLEMENTATION: 
A body of students shall be formed whose purpose shall be to function as the Student Honor Council. 
A. Membership
1. The Student Honor Council shall consist of twenty-five members. . ,
2 The Council shall be selected by an interview board composed of the Student Body President, the Chairman of the Blue Circle, the Class Presidents, the College Senators, the Editor 
of the Scholastic, the Editor of the Voice and the Station Manager of WSND. . 
3. 
The interview board shall select at least one man rrom each of the three upper classes in ea:h college and the remaining thirteen from the student body at large. 

4. 
The Council shall select its own officers. 


B. Duties 
1. 
The Council shall publish the Honor Code before every final exam period and at the beginning of each academic year. 

2. 
The Council shall constantly work to maintain cooperation among students, faculty, and administration. 

3. 
The Council shall recommend amendments to the Honor Code to the Student Senate. 

4. 
The Council shall deal fairly with reported violations accord­ing to the provisions of the Honor Code. 

5. 
The Council shall keep complete records of each case which 


shall be destroyed after the student’s departure from the University. 
6. Officers: 
a) Chairman who will: Preside over the Council Call meetings . 
Preside at every trial without having a vote himself. 
b) 
Recording secretary 

c) 
Corresponding secretary who will: 


Maintain correspondence with other schools Be responsible for publicity to the Student Body. 
PROCEDURES: Article \ 
A. The Instructor . 
In cooperation with the spirit of the Honor Code, the in­structor shall assume the honesty of his students and shall not act as a proctor during an examination. 
1. 
After an initial ten-minute period, it is requested that the instructor be absent from the examination room. 

2. 
The instructor is requested to make himself available in a manner convenient to himself and to his students, in order to answer any questions that may arise during the remainder of the examination.
